            (function($) {
                var timer;
                $("#edition_nav, #region_nav").click(function() {
                    $(this).toggleClass("edition_nav_selected");
                }).mouseleave(function(){
                    var e = $(this);
                    timer && clearTimeout(timer);
                    timer = setTimeout(function(){
                        e.hasClass('edition_nav_selected') && e.removeClass('edition_nav_selected')
                    }, 1000);
                }).mouseenter(function(){
                timer && clearTimeout(timer);
                });
            })(jQuery);

																		<span itemprop="articleBody">
									<p>BEIJING &mdash; China's leaders are finding it's a lot tougher to create a world-beating electric car industry than they hoped.</p>

<p>In 2009, they announced bold plans to cash in on demand for clean vehicles by making China a global power in electric car manufacturing. They pledged billions of dollars for research and called for annual sales of 500,000 cars by 2015.</p>
									<p>Today, Beijing is scaling back its ambitions, chastened by technological hurdles and lack of buyer interest. Developers have yet to achieve breakthroughs and will be lucky to sell 2,000 cars this year, mostly taxis. The government has hedged its bets by broadening the industry's official goals to include cleaner gasoline engines.</p>

<p>The government has repeatedly changed targets because the "technology isn't advancing quite as fast as people had hoped," said Joe Hinrichs, Ford Motor Co.'s president for Asia, at this week's Beijing auto show.</p>

<p>The government has yet to lower sales goals that ramp up to 5 million vehicles a year by 2020. But officials including Premier Wen Jiabao started acknowledging last year that progress was slow and developers need to improve quality instead of rushing models to market.</p>

<p>About 13,000 all-electric and other alternative energy vehicles are being tested in 25 cities, but that is "still small despite government subsidies," the deputy director of the Ministry of Science and Technology's electric vehicle bureau, Zhen Zijian, said in March, according to the business magazine Caixin.</p>

<p>China's most advanced developer, BYD Co., in which American investor Warren Buffett's Berkshire Hathaway Corp. owns a 10 percent stake, says its electric e6 sedan can travel 300 kilometers (190 miles) on a charge, similar to Western models.</p>

<p>BYD has sold 300 taxis and 200 electric buses used in the southern city of Shenzhen, a center for business and technology near Hong Kong, according to Henry Li, general manager of its export division. BYD has invested heavily in research and has thousands of engineers working on battery and motor technology.</p>

<p>"We think our EV (electric vehicle) platform is one of the most advanced in the world, and our capability for mass production is quite high," Li said.</p>

	<div id="ad_mid_article" class="ad_wrapper">                    <script type="text/javascript">
                        if(HPAds.ad_check_page_config('mid_article')) {
                            var adId = 'null';
                            HPAds.adSonar("1570394", "2930767", "300", "250");
                            var debugadcode = '';
                            document.write(debugadcode);
                        }
                    </script></div><p>But as for the rest of the industry, "there are not many manufacturers with really reliable or commercialized products," he said.</p>

<p>Chinese leaders saw electric cars as a way to curb demand for imported oil, which they regard as a strategic danger, and to help transform China from a low-cost factory into a creator of profitable technology.</p>

<p>"China has run up against the same technical obstacles as anyone else," said Michael Dunne, president of Dunne & Co. Ltd., a Hong Kong-based industry researcher.</p>

<p>"They said: Hold on, maybe we shouldn't marry ourselves to electrics just yet. Let's look at the alternatives. Maybe we have to take an incremental approach, just like everyone else," Dunne said.</p>

<p>Wary consumers have been put off by news reports of batteries in Chinese-made cars catching fire. A lack of charging stations is causing "range anxiety" &ndash; fears a car might run out of power, leaving the driver stranded.</p>

<p>Under the Communist Party's latest five-year development plan for China's economy, issued in 2011, the government has released guidelines for other industries but not for alternative vehicles &ndash; a possible sign officials have gone back to the drawing board.</p>

<p>Developers were encouraged last week by a Cabinet statement that repeated support for electric vehicles. But it also called for work on developing non-plug-in hybrids and energy-saving internal combustion engines.</p>

<p>"The momentum has been slowed down," said John Zeng, chief of Asian forecasting for LMC Automotive, a research firm.</p>

<p>"They don't expect the EV or hybrid can be the only way for China to maintain its future sustainable mobility," Zeng said. "They think they need multiple initiatives to achieve that target."</p>

<p>Plus, gasoline and diesel technologies are advancing, luring consumers with the promise of lower operating costs.</p>

<p>U.S. sales of electric cars have also been disappointing. After a year on the market, electric cars still make up less than 1 percent of total U.S. sales. General Motors Co. fell short of its goal of selling 10,000 Chevrolet Volt electric cars in 2011, ending up with sales just over 7,500. Nissan sold 9,674 Leaf electric cars, also short of its goal of 10,000.</p>

<p>As in China, the lack of a recharging infrastructure and anxiety about the range of electric cars are big barriers for consumers. Cost is another issue. The Chevrolet Volt, for example, costs nearly $8,000 more than the similarly sized gas-powered Chevrolet Cruze. Auto shopping site Edmunds.com estimates it would take a Volt owner six years of gas savings to pay off that premium.</p>

<p>The Chinese government launched research into electric, fuel cell and other alternative power sources in 2001. It followed in 2004 with a plan to create a competitive electric car and promised financial support to developers.</p>

<p>Automakers responded to Beijing's enthusiasm. General Motors Co. announced plans in 2007 for a $250 million alternative fuel research center in Shanghai. Germany's Daimler AG teamed up with BYD to create an electric car joint venture dubbed Denza. They unveiled a display version of its first model this week at the Beijing auto show.</p>

<p>China's initiative prompted some in the United States and Europe to worry they might fall behind in a key technology. An assistant U.S. energy secretary, David Sandalow, visited Beijing in 2009 and warned China had "the potential to be ahead" if the United States failed to invest in development.</p>

<p>Beijing's 2009 plan called for world-class electric cars by this year, followed by trucks and buses. To encourage buyers, the government started paying buyers rebates of up to 60,000 yuan ($8,800) per car the following year in five cities including Shanghai.</p>

<p>But Wen, China's top economic official, expressed frustration at the slow pace of development in an article published last July.</p>

<p>"We are no match for developed countries in technology," Wen wrote in Qiushi, the ruling party's main theoretical journal.</p>

<p>"We've only just begun in electric car development," the premier wrote. Wen said Chinese leaders shared in the blame: "We have not set clear enough goals of which way to go."</p>

<p>Beijing strained relations with the United States and other trading partners by rolling out rules limiting access to its auto market unless foreign developers shared technology to Chinese partners.</p>

<p>Daimler has said it formed its venture with BYD not due to official pressure but because it wanted to create a low-cost brand for China. Daimler said their car, due to go on sale next year, should have a range of 200-250 kilometers (125-155 miles) on one charge.</p>

<p>Other manufacturers such as Nissan Motor Co., maker of the electric Leaf, and General Motors Co. have chosen to pay the higher taxes required to import electric and hybrid vehicles rather than disclose expensive know-how to Chinese partners that might become rivals.</p>

<p>GM is taking orders for its all-electric Volt in China but expects limited sales due to a relatively high price of 498,000 yuan ($79,000).</p>

<p>"It's expensive in China at the moment because of import duties, and we don't qualify for incentives," said Kevin Wale, president of GM China. "But we still think it's important that we demonstrate its capabilities here in China."</p>

<p>Chinese producers have unveiled a series of display models of electric and hybrid cars, some sprouting tiny solar panels or wind turbines for recharging, though most say they are not ready for mass-market sales.</p>

<p>LMC Automotive's Zeng said that aside from BYD, which has spent heavily on development, most have done only the minimum required to qualify for research grants.</p>

<p>"I think it's more to create a PR bubble or fight for government subsidies," he said.</p>

	                                <strong><a  href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/lisa-kaas-boyle/power-the-world_b_1447817.html">Lisa Kaas Boyle: Power the World</a></strong><br>
                                </p>
		                				                            <div style="padding-left:49px;">
		                        
																For most Americans, most of the time, electricity is a given. We rely on electricity to power our lives at work, at school and at home. We rely on it so much, it comes as quite a shock when we are deprived of it.                            </div>
		                		
                            </div>

				Lithium Rush: The Art Of War In The Markets: China Getting Ready For 5 Million Electric Cars by 2020<br />
<br />
China has the money, political will and the technology to leapfrog into the post carbon world. Oil is the geopolitical issue already and it will define the sharp edge between the state of War and Peace in the nearest future. As one very wise and honest  person has put it: "How to stop wars and terrorism? - Stop using Oil." We will paraphrase it here: How to Survive? - Stop using Oil - at least for transportation.<br />
Electric Cars produce the one life time opportunity for China now - do not get us wrong, not everything is driven by the ancient wisdom of "The Art Of War", but just look at what people are doing and not what they are talking about.  It is the most apparent situation  in the strategic commodities markets - Rare Earths are already controlled by China, Graphite is under the siege and Lithium is the next frontier. Despite all noise in the media, China is steadily implementing its 12th Five Year Plan - to build the new strategic industry based on Electric Cars.<br />
We hope, that China is transforming "The Art Of War" into the Art Of Survival for the benefit of all, but the Western world which is teared apart by the latest financial structural crisis is falling dangerously behind now.<br />
<br />
<a href="http://sufiy.blogspot.co.uk/2012/04/lithium-rush-china-getting-ready-for-5.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">http://sufiy.blogspot.co.uk/2012/04/lithium-rush-china-getting-ready-for-5.html</a>#			</div>

			});

	Comments.topicDir = '';

	if (HuffCookies.getUserName() ) {
		// change the post button

		button_logged = document.getElementById('post_button_for_logged_in');
		button_not_logged = document.getElementById('post_button_for_not_logged_in');
		if (button_logged && button_not_logged) {
			button_logged.style.display = 'none';
			button_not_logged.style.display = 'block';
		}

			}


	if (typeof(CommentsLoader.setListeners) !== "undefined") {
		CommentsLoader.setListeners();
	}

	var update_time_interval = 30000;
	if (HPConfig.comments_update_interval || HPConfig.comments_update_interval === 0) {
		update_time_interval = HPConfig.comments_update_interval;
	}

	var update_comments = false;
	// should we update comments for everyone ?
	if (HPConfig.comments_update_for_all_users === true) {
		// yes, for everyone
		update_comments = true;
	} else {
		// no - then maybe your user is logged in ?
		if (HPConfig.comments_update_for_all_users === false && HuffCookies.getUserName()) {
			// yes, logged in - we may update comments
			update_comments = true;
		}
	}
	if (update_comments === true) {
		setTimeout("CommentPollerV3.check(1448305, true);", update_time_interval);
	}

<script type="text/javascript">
	/* use hot keys for slidehow */
		
    // add to body browser type
    jQuery('body').addClass(HPBrowser.browser_class().toLowerCase() + (HPBrowser.version() + '').replace('.', '-'));

<!-- Sailthru Horizon 'World'--> 
<script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        function loadHorizon() { 
            var s = document.createElement('script'); 
            s.type = 'text/javascript'; 
            s.async = true;
            s.src = location.protocol + '//ak.sail-horizon.com/horizon/v1.js';
            var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0]; 
            x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
        }
        loadHorizon();
        var oldOnLoad = window.onload;
        window.onload = function() {

            var vertical_name = 'World';
            var vertical_color = HPConfig.current_vertical_color;

            if (typeof oldOnLoad === 'function') {
                oldOnLoad();
            }
            Sailthru.setup({
                domain: 'horizon.huffingtonpost.com',
                            concierge: {
                    from: 'top',
                    threshold: jQuery('.email-alert-sbm'),
                    cssPath: 'http://' + HPConfig.hp_static_domain + '/assets/css.php?f=sailthru_concierge.css&v=v1',
                    offsetBottom: 10,
                    filter: { tags: vertical_name }
                }
                        });

                    var style_modification = setInterval(function(){

                var recommendation = jQuery('.recommendation');
                if ( recommendation.length > 0 ) {

                    //removing 'HuffPost' from vertical name
                    vertical_name = jQuery.trim(vertical_name.replace(/huffpost/i, ''));
                
                    //changing style to vertical default
                    recommendation.css('border-top-color', vertical_color);
                    jQuery('.recommendationCategory').html('More in ' + vertical_name);
                    jQuery('.recommendationTitle a').css('color', vertical_color);
                    jQuery('.recommendationFooter').css('display', 'none');

                    var img = jQuery('.recommendationThumb img');

                    //if there's no image -> alternative layout
                    var alt_layout = ( img.size() == 0 );

                    //if image smaller size -> alternative layout
                    if( !alt_layout ) {

                        alt_layout = ( img[0].naturalWidth < img.width() 
                                    || img[0].naturalHeight < img.height() ); 
                             
                    }

                    if ( alt_layout ) {
                        jQuery('.recommendationThumb').css('display', 'none');
                        jQuery('.recommendationDetails').css('width', '100%');
                    }

                    //adding tracking parameters
                    jQuery('#sailthru-concierge').attr('data-beacon', '{"p":{"mnid":"sailthru_rec"}}');
                    jQuery('a.openRecommendation').attr('data-beacon','{"p":{"lnid":"open_flyout"}}');
                    jQuery('a.closeRecommendation').attr('data-beacon','{"p":{"lnid":"close_flyout"}}');
                    
                    //adding 'bN class to fire click() event
                    jQuery('.recommendationThumb a, .recommendationDetails a').addClass('bN');
              
                    clearInterval(style_modification);
                }
            }, 500);
            
            //once the flyout is shown -> send ping()
            var ping = setInterval( function() {
                
                if ( jQuery('.recommendation').css('display') == 'block' ) { 
                    bN.ping('sailthru_concierge');
                    clearInterval(ping);
                }

            }, 500);
                };
    })();
</script>
